-=Procedural Learning=
-
-
-
-== Skill Acquisition ==
-
-
-=== Skill ===
-[[Image:CoryPesaturo1.jpg|thumb|Playing the accordion requires procedural skills]]
-A '''skill''' can be defined as one's attempt to make a behavioural change or learn a desired task using the least amount of energy and time. This is often achieved through repetition, with the end result being a smooth and seemingly effortless execution of an activity Yamadori, A, et al (1996). Neurological Basis for Skill Learning. Cognitive Brain Research, 5, 49-55.. An example of this would be the learning of an instrument- though very difficult at first, repetition creates competence and an ease of movement. Thus a [[skill]] can only improve with practice. http://www.exrx.net/Psychology/Skill.html For one to acquire a new [[skill]] one travels through the three stages of skill acquisition and eventually ends up moving from being a [[novice]] to an [[expert]] (see below).
-
-It has been suggested that memory for self-performed tasks is much better than for memories that are just verbal tasks. Koriat, K. &Pearlman-Avnion, S. (2003). Memory organization of action events and its relationship to memory performance. Journal of Experimental Psychology: General. 132 (3) This appears to be the case because of the enactment effect, or the memory for actions. For example, the enactment effect stresses that there are representational differences between verbal tasks and self-promotion tasks. This is because task performance involves both [[recall]] and [[recognition]] of action phases in comparison to the encoding of a verbal phrase. Also enactment requires the planning, programming, and execution of tasks rather than just verbalizing it. Therefore, the enactment heightens the features of a task. Furthermore, there is evidence that the intention to perform a task greatly improves the memory performance later on. The amount of errors in performance also decreases with enactment as memory is enhanced by reducing the number of false recalls. In addition, self-performed tasks are encoded at the same rate with or without attention and with deep or shallow processing, which indicates that these type of tasks are largely automatic. Classen, J., Joachim, L., Wise, S. P., Hallett, M. & Cohen ,L. G. (1998). Rapid plasticity of human cortical movement representation induced by practice. Journal of Neurophysiology, 79, 1117-1123
-
-=== Cognitive Stage ===
-
-This is the first stage of skill acquisition in which an individual has complete conscious awareness and is striving to obtain the skill. Full attention is generally necessary at this stage and thus [[declarative memory]] holds the representation of the skillNewell & Simon (1972): General Problem Solver. The main goal at this stage is to take whatever actions are needed to get from the place where they are at currently to the mastery of the skill. A lot of visual and verbal guidance and practice in the form of trial and error are used extensively to help move closer to the mastery of a skill. To use a musician as an example, they would be seen as novice or even non-musician at this stage. They are generally learning the basics and need specific instructions from instructors to help them correct there errors as the student will not often know how to correct it themselves. Gaser C., Schlaug, G. (2003) Brain structures differ between musicians and non-musicians. The Journal of Neuroscience, 23,(27), 9240-9245
-
-=== Associative Stage ===
-
-This is the second stage of skill acquisition and at this stage the person is still consciously aware of what is taking place. However, information is retrieved much quicker and less deliberate attention is needed. The skill is now moving into [[procedural memory]] as movements become much more fluid and contain fewer errors. The associative stage is also known as the practice stage where events are repeated over and over to create [[overlearning]] or a [[perma-store]] of the skill. If we use the musician again as an example, the musician would now be seen as an amateur or intermediate as they have mastered the basics but still require much more practice in order to be considered a master. The instructor or teacher in this stage is needed to provide the learner with additional information focusing on specific actions and helpful pointers for fine-tuning.
-
-=== Autonomous Stage ===
-
-This is the third and final stage in skill acquisition and at this point the skill has moved from being conscious to largely unconscious. This is to say that this skill is now part of [[procedural memory]]. Performance of the skill has been automatized and rapid cognitive monitoring becomes almost completely eliminated. With respect to the musician example, they would now be seen as a professional or master. They are now able to perform in an automatic fashion without stress, and begin to strategize rather than worrying about whether they will play the right tune or not. The instructor or teacher only needs to facilitate learning as the student will have the knowledge to correct their own errors if made.
-
-== '''Motor Learning''' ==
-
-
-
-[[Motor learning]] is a general term found within the domain of skill acquisition and incorporates learning muscle movements within sequences and then repeating them until they can be performed without hesitation or thought processing. An example of this is a triathlete training in cycling, running and swimming who must train their muscles to operate in certain ways for the most time efficient race Chapman, A. R., Vicenzio, B., Blanch, P., Dowlan, S., & Hodges , P. W. (2008). Does cycling effect motor coordination of the leg during running in elite triathletes? Journal of Science and Medicine in Sport, 11, 371-380..This is quite often thought of as [[muscle memory]], which is a misnomer as motor learning refers to the cognitive processes that drive a body to interact with the world Koriat, K. & Pearlman-Avnion, S. (2003). Memory organization of action events and its relationship to memory performance. Journal of Experimental Psychology: General. 132 (3). Motor learning, like skill acquisition, is best done with enactment, which can increase one’s attention to the salient features of a task leading to an increase in memory performance and thus a decrease in the number of errors .
-
-Due to the cognitive nature of motor learning there is some neural reorganization and activation/deactivation in the brain before, during and after the motor task becomes fluent Duque, J., Mazzocchio, R., Stefan, K., Hummel, F., Olivier, E. & Cohen, L. G. (2008). Memory formation in the motor cortex ipsilateral to a training hand. Cerebral Cortex, 18, 1395-1406.. This reorganization is thought to involve [[long-term potentiation]] that supports learning and memory Classen, J., Joachim, L., Wise, S. P., Hallett, M. & Cohen ,L. G. (1998). Rapid plasticity of human cortical movement representation induced by practice. Journal of Neurophysiology, 79, 1117-1123.. This cortical reorganization generally occurs in the motor cortices on the [[contralateral]] side, or side opposite the part of the body being used . However some [[ipsilateral]], or the same side of the brain regions involved for carrying out those motor movements, cortical encoding does occur. Therefore there are memory traces developing in the motor areas of the brain with practice . These memory traces make later enactment of the movement much easier.
-
-Motor learning of tasks occurs in several phases, much like skill acquisition, except the focus is on the motor movements of a task and repetition. The first stage includes rapid performance gains over the initial few trials and corresponds to the acquisition of a task-relevant routine. This usually includes such cortical areas as the [[prefrontal cortex]], anterior [[cingulate cortex]], and the posterior [[parietal lobe]] Clare Kelly, A. M. & Garavan, H. (2004) . Following this there is a stage of consolidation which can last several hours . The final stage is repetition, which requires significantly more time than the first two stages. This is because as repetition of the movement occurs there is a slower pace at which the movement is mastered due the adjustments that are consistently made to perfect the movement. These adjustments are achieved through sensory and motor pathways providing continuous feedback. Thousands of training trails are required and are associated with expansion or increases in activation in motor areas of the brain, as well as differing levels of activation throughout the motor regions. Most motor skills can be overlearned to the point where they are almost implicit and do not need conscious effort to perform the taskUnderleider, L. G., Doyon, J., & Karni, A. (2002). Imaging brain plasticity during motor skill learning. Neurobiology Learning and Memory, 78, 553-564.
-
-Peripheral to the central nervous system there are control mechanisms that have been found in motor control studies. For example, the use of reciprocally activating sets of antagonist and agonist muscles that can produce torques on a desired joint. This cocontraction is in flux when a novel motor task is being performed which leads to overlap in muscle use. A balance between antagonist and agonist muscle can be found leading to no kinematic effect, and therefore no movement Darainy, M. & Ostry, D. J. (2008). Muscle cocontraction following dynamics learning. Experimental Brain Research, 190, 153-163. . This cocontraction control has been documented in the early stages of motor learning with a decline as learning progresses; however, it is never fully absent, indicating the need for continuous adaptation . The cocontraction often last for several hundred milliseconds after motor movement has terminated, demonstrating the lasting effects of learning in muscle memory .
-
-
-=== '''Motor Memory by Observation''' ===
-
-The ipsilateral hemisphere to the arm that is learning a task plays a role in the learning but it is not as strong as the dominant contraleteral hemisphere Crischimagna-Hemminger, S. E., Donchon, O., Gazzaniga, M. S., & Shadmeher, R. (2003). Learned dynamics of reaching movements generalize from dominant to non-dominant arm. Journal of Neurophysiology, 89, 167-176..
-This is similar to learning by observation and learning with physical practice. These types of learning can be compared with cortical imaging.
-For example, the primary motor cortex (M1) and other motor cortices contain specific neurons that are activated during movement, as they are sensitive to the pattern of forces and posture of limbs, as well as to the observations of said movements . Although motor skills are acquired through physical practice, the mere observation of movements has also been shown to lead to performance gains Karni, A., Meyer, G., Rey-Hipolito, C., Jezzard, P., Adams, M. M., Turner, R., & Underleider, L. G. (1998). The acquisition of skills motor performances: fast and slow experience-driven changes in primary motor cortex. Proc National Academy of Science, USA, 95, 861-868. . Mere observation of movements can lead to the formation of lasting memory traces in movement representations that resemble memory traces developed with physical training; this is termed ‘observation-induced motor memory’ . The formation of motor memory is initiated with observation and thus it acts as an important step for motor skill acquisition. Therefore, observational practice may improve performance through the use of similar mechanisms in physical training Stefan, K., Cohen, L. G., Duque, J., Mazzocchio, R., Celnik, P., Sawaki, L., Ungerleider, L., & Classen, J. (2005). Formation of motor memory by action observation. Journal of Neuroscience, 25 (41), 9339-9346.
-
-== '''Plasticity''' ==
-
-A study by Gaser and Schlaug Gaser, C., & Schlaug, G. (2003). Brain structures differ between musicians and non-musicians. The Journal of Neuroscience, 23(27), 9240-9245. found that there is a significant difference in terms of [[gray matter]] volume in the superior parietal (visual-spatial), inferior temporal gyrus, primary motor cortex, cerebellum, hippocampus, and auditory brain regions of professional musicians compared to amateur or non-musicians. Although [[white matter]] does not appear to be influenced by procedural memory training glial cells have been observed to increase in volume. While plausible that such gray matter volume differences may arise from genetic predispositions rather than experience, meaning that perhaps individuals select their professions (in part at least) based on the morphology of their brains, the literature suggests that the differences observed are likely the result of [[synaptic plasticity]] and learning .
-
-
-= Anatomy of Procedural Learning =
-
-== '''Brain Regions Associated with Skill Acquisition and Motor Learning''' ==
-
-
-The present understanding of the association between learning a motor skill and cortical changes remains debated and difficult to establish; however, with recent advances in technology, researchers are able to study the brain while actions are being performed, for example, when reaching for objects or experiencing rotating visual stimuli. Thus motor learning studies use imaging technologies such as [[positron emission tomography]] (PET) Nilsson et al, 2000), functional [[magnetic resonance imaging]] (fMRI) , [[transcranial magnetic stimulation]] (TMS) Kolb, B. Whishaw, I. Q. (2003). Fundamentals of Human Neuropsychology, 5th Ed. Worth Publishers, New York, New York.,and near-infrared spectroscopy (NIRS), which is used to measure cerebral hemoglobin oxygenation in the sensorimotor cortices of both hemispheres . In conjunction with cortical imaging, motor skill learning is often investigated through measurement of reduction in reaction times and number of errors and/or by a change in movement synergy and kinematics .
-
-Generally as skills are practiced there are related decreases in brain activity, which reflect the efficient use of specific neuronal circuits that are topographically organized . For example, when learning how to tap a sequence with one’s fingers there is an increase in the neuronal activity, thus indicating the recruitment of additional cortical units, or the strengthening response of a particular region to complete the task . As the sequence tapping become less effortful there is a corresponding decrease in cortical activity.
-
-Behavioural studies have shown that the brain might update the mechanism for sensorimotor control in every trial that they do with a novel task Donchin, O., Francis, J. T., & Shadmehr, R. (2003). Quantifying generalization from trial-by-trial behavior of adaptive systems that learn with basis functions: Theory and experiments in human motor control, The Journal of Neuroscience 23(27), 9032–9045.. Generally models looking at motor learning in this way use discrete movements that are constricted by specific postures. In this way they are different from rhythmic or sequential movements because they require a start and stop to the movement and thus go in small bursts of movement .Some examples of discrete movements would be reaching to grasp an object, or kicking or striking a ball.
-
-
-[[Image:Kendama.jpg|thumb|Kendama Toy]]
-
-Researchers Ikegami and Taga (2008) used the [[Kendama]] toy to assess the motor learning for using multiple joints in a particular pattern to get to an end result, for example a motor task completed with a tool. This tool requires a quick and dynamic movement of the hand to swing the ball attached to the string into the cup. This is a novel task that requires precise manipulation of the tool in combination with multi-joint control, and eye-hand coordination. The initial stages of this task are quite difficult; however, this changes with practice trials and performance improves Ikegami, T. & Taga, G. (2008). Decrease in cortical activation during learning of multi-joint discrete motor task. Experimental Brain Research, 191, 221-236.. This type of motor learning is associated with contralateral left sensorimotor cortex activation and decreases with practice. This reduction in cortical activation correlates with the decrease in integrated muscle torques of the upper limb, or the arm being used to swing the ball into the cup. This indicates that changes in motor commands play a role in generating the muscle torques used to effectively perform the task and indicates that less sensory input needed to successfully perform a task . Therefore the more motor learning that takes place, the less cortical activity is needed to perform a task.
-
-The motor cortex is strongly involved with motor learning, and researchers Kolb and Winshaw (2005) used TMS to map this activity during learning. As a skill is learned, the cortical area of the [[motor cortex]] is enlarged and this enlargement corresponds to the area of the body being used . The changes in the structure of the motor cortex cannot be detected by an MRI until a few weeks after motor learning has had many repeated trials; however, differences from before learning and after learning are significant . During the learning process, PET can be utilized to see that both the left [[parietal]] and motor cortex are activated and cortical reorganization of the primary motor cortex (M1) is evident during the initial stages of skill acquisition . Thus the process of acquiring implicit knowledge requires a reorganization of the motor cortex .
-
-Classen, Joachim, Wise, Hallett & Cohen (1998) found that practicing fingers movements in a particular direction leaves a short-lasting memory trace in the [[contralateral]] M1 and these changes are linked to the types and magnitude of motor action Perez, M. A. & Cohen, L. G. (2008). Mechanisms underlying functional changes in the primary motor cortex [[ipsilateral]] to an active hand. The Journal of Neuroscience, 28(22), 5631-5640.. There is some evidence of ipsilateral activity-dependant adaptation in M1 as well, however not to the same extent as the contralateral side Van Mier, H., Tempel, L. W., Perlmutter, J. S., Raichle, M. E., & Petersen, S. E. (1998). Changes in brain activity during motor learning measured with PET: effects of hand of performance and practice. Journal of Neurophysiology, 80, 381-391.. This rapid M1 plasticity occurs through synaptic modification of the local horizontal circuitry, which is modulated through [[NMDA]] receptors. These changes are made permanent with long-term potentiation and long-term depression that act as up and down regulators depending on the pattern of activity.
-
-Other regions of the brain have been associated with skill acquisition. For example, in the early phase of learning there is significant activity in the [[cerebellum]], right anterior [[cingulate]], dorsal premotor, and inferior parietal regions. However, as practice continues, the cerebellar and cortical regions decrease their level of activity, and as movements become automatic, activity remains in the striatum and motor cortical regions Radvansky,G.(2006)''Human Memory''. University of Notre Dame: Pearson Education. Furthermore, the [[striatum]] appears to play a large role in the use of cognitive strategies and working memory with extended practice, and from this it seems likely that it plays a large role in long-term storage of well-learned sequences of movements .
-
-The cerebellum plays a particularly interesting role in the stages of skill acquisition such that it has been attributed to sensory prediction (the ability to maintain a continual flow in our movements and our perceptions of the world by responding to a stimulus with a prediction for the next stimulus), as well as the ability to process and learn from visual inputSaywell,N.(2008).The role of the cerebellum in procedural learning--are there implications for physiotherapists' clinical practice? ''Physiotherapy Theory and Practice''. 24, 321-328. ; for example, by watching someone use a tool, which is a motor skill, you are better able to use it yourself.
-
-The cerebellum is also an important area of the brain for the commitment and retrieval of procedural memories. It has often been called a "comparator" because it detects mistakes in movement by comparing them to aspects of the skill that have been learned and remembered, thus refining the habit or skill that is requiredSaywell,N.(2008).The role of the cerebellum in procedural learning--are there implications for physiotherapists' clinical practice? ''Physiotherapy Theory and Practice''. 24, 321-328. . Memory retrieval is necessary for procedural learning, because without retrieval, it would be impossible to achieve sensory prediction.
-
-The [[basal ganglia]] is another cortical structure involved in procedural memory. It has been observed through numerous studies that people with damage to this area (especially in degenerative cases such as [[dementia]]) have extreme difficulty in performing procedural tasks such as tennis, sewing, or playing piano, but often have remarkably less problems with tasks involving [[declarative memory]]Gonzalez, R., et al. (2008). Deficits in Complex Motor Functions, Despite No Evidence of Procedural Learning Deficits, Among HIV Individuals With History of Substance Dependence. American Psychological Association, 22. 776-786.
-
-The cortical activation becomes more complex when comparing regions that are active during different stages of learning. For example, there is a high level of activation of the right dorsal premotor cortex during initial unskilled performance of a task, which is mainly guided by external sensory cues . Activation of the supplementary motor area is greater during skilled performance, and this stage of learning is self-initiated and guided by internal cues . Furthermore, left cerebellar activation decreases with practice and is highly active with novel tasks . The right dorsal premotor cortex and supplementary motor area are associated with sequential aspects of a task. This is in contrast with the left dorsal premotor cortex and the right cerebellum which are more likely to be associated with the temporal aspects of a task .
-
-Overall, the areas that are directly related with motor performance and learning are the primary motor cortex, anterior cerebellum, basal ganglia and striatum.
-
-=Affecting Procedural Memory=
-
-As procedural memory, and implicit non-declarative forms of memory in general, are distinct from declarative memory it is both important and very interesting to look at the ways in which procedural memory and skill acquisition can be impacted. Repeated findings in studies have shown that impairments to procedural memory are generally independent of compromised declarative memory, and vice versa Yamadori, A, et al (1996). Neurological Basis for Skill Learning. Cognitive Brain Research, 5, 49-55.. Thus, while some illnesses and traumas may affect procedural memory, declarative memory can potentially remain in tact. The following examples show the various ways that procedural learning can be altered, or not.
-
-== The Impact of Disease on Procedural Memory ==
-Many impairments to procedural memory occur because of health conditions that are degenerative to neural anatomy pertinent to implicit memory and skill acquisition.
-
-[[Parkinson's Disease]]- Parkinson's Disease (PD) is a condition that affects the efficiency of procedural memory and skills acquisition. Those with PD, especially elderly individuals, score much lower than healthy individuals (old and young) on procedural memory tasks such as sound-form association, mazes, and Braille learning. It has been found that while PD affects both implicit and explicit memories Allain H, et al (1995). Explicit and Procedural Memory in Parkinson’s Disease. Biomedicine & Parkinson’s Disease, 49, 179-186. implicit memory is more drastically impaired McDowall, John, Jared, G. Smith. Impaired Higher Order Implicit Sequence Learning on the Verbal Version of the Serial Reaction Time Task in Patients with Parkinson’s Disease. Neuropsychology, 18, 679-691. PD patients' deficiency in procedural memory tasks has been theorized to be the result of an enhancement of memory inhibition. This means that people with PD may only be able to operate with newer memories, making practice a useless endeavor. Also, because of damage to various areas in the brain made by PD, studies have shown that there may be disruption in the steps of learning, automation and recall, making fluid motor skills difficult . One of these areas is the basal ganglia, which has been previously discussed as being implicated in skill acquisition. Dopamine deficiencies, which are linked to procedural memory, are also found in PD patients .
-
-[[Huntington's Disease]]- Huntington's Disease (HD) is a disorder that involves involuntary movements and eventual dementia. HD patients show impaired ability to recall information that they have previously been exposed to or learned
-Heindel, W, Butters, N., Salmon D. (1988). Impaired Learning of A Motor Skill In Patients with Huntington’s Disease, 102. 141-147, and perform at a less than normal level in certain procedural skill tasks. Akin to other conditions that impair procedural memory and skill acquisition, HD's affect on the basal ganglia is also associated with lack of ability in skill learningCavaco,S (2007). Procedural Memory in Huntington's Disease. World Congress on Huntington's Disease. http://www.worldcongress-hd.net/html/2007/programme/wchd2007-programme-booklet.pdf?tm=1195018831. While it has been established that the neurological degeneration characteristic of HD bring about issues in procedural learning, some of this difficulty may be partly to do with HD patients' general motor dysfunction
-
-==Psychological Disorders and Procedural Memory==
-
-[[Bipolar disorder]] - Bipolar disorder is categorized by unusual shifts in a person’s mood, ranging from bouts of mania to depression http://www.nimh.nih.gov/health/publications/bipolar-disorder/complete-index.shtml. The exact causes of bipolar disorder is not completely known but results from tests on procedural memory suggest that bipolar disorder most likely involves a distributed function of the temporal lobe, but not the basal ganglia. The result of this is that bipolar patients have a deficit in declarative memory but no loss of procedural memory as compared to individuals without the disorderVan Gorp, W.G., Altshuler, L., Theberge, D.C., Mintz, J. (1999). Declarative and Procedural Memory in Bipolar Disorder. Biological psychiatry, 46. 525-531
-
-[[Psychosis]] - Psychosis is reflected by a disturbance in brain functioning that often involves a loss of contact with reality. http://www.cmha.ca/BINS/content_page.asp?cid=3-105 Similar to those suffering from bipolar disorder, individuals with some forms of psychosis are able to perform motor procedural learning tasks at the same level as those not suffering from a psychosis. They also show no deficits in cognitive or motor procedural learning. Schmond, B., Brand, N., Kuipers, T. (1992). Procedural learning of cognitive and motor skills in psychotic patients. Schizophrenia Research, 8. 157-170 Interestingly when psychotic patients were asked to learn the rules of a game, they were actually able to learn the rules much better and made less error than those who do did not suffer from psychosis. [[Schizophrenia]] is a type of psychosis that is categorized by the [[DSM-IV-TR]] as breaks from reality that may include but are not limited to delusions and hallucinations. http://www.cmha.ca/BINS/content_page.asp?cid=3-100&lang=1 Notably individuals suffering from this disorder have shown a shallower learning slope, meaning that they learned less then control groups in tests measuring declarative memory. However, individuals with schizophrenia have similar learning slopes or show approximately the same amount of learning as people without schizophrenia when tested on procedural memory tasks.
-
-[[Amnesia]] - Amnesia is a condition that effects the tenacity of memory as well as the ability to use it and it can have a very localized effect on the brain and memory. More specifically, it has been found that [[anterograde amnesia] -a condition that inhibits the formation of new memories- primarily effects the [[medial temporal lobe]], thus almost exclusively impairing declarative memory. Studies have shown that not only is amnesia in such patients not complete, but it also preserves near normal-to-normal levels of perceptual-motor skill acquisition Cavaco, S. et al (2004). The scope of preserved procedural memory in amnesia. Brain, 127. 8, pp. 1853-1867. Similarly, in the famous case of the amnesiac [[HM]], it was found that his basal ganglia- a section of brain anatomy important for procedural memory- was normal, and that in tests of his ability for procedural memory, learning also seemed normal Xu, Yaoda, Corkin, Suzanna (2001).H.M. Revisits the Tower of Hanoi Puzzle, 15, 69-79. Another excellent example of the durability of procedural memory in anterograde amnesiacs is in the musician [[Clive Wearing]]. Wearing was a classical musician who suffered from encephalitis resultant of the herpes simplex virus; while he could not remember someone whom he had only met minutes ago, Wearing could still play piano or conduct music with much the same skill as he could before the onset of amnesia . Anterograde amnesia is therefore interesting because it helps to show us the difference between declarative and non-declarative memory, showing a preservation in procedural memory; this effect is also seen in [[retrograde amnesia]], or the forgetting of memories previous to an amnesia-inducing incident, though are not quite as pristine as with anterograde amnesia .
-''Children with Amnesia:'' Similar to adults who suffer from amnesia, children show deficits on both episodic and semantic memory but in the past there have been questions regarding whether or not procedural memory would be affected differently in a younger population. However, test results show that children with amnesia do not differ in procedural memory from their adult counterparts with procedural memory remaining unaffected in cases of children with amnesia.Ostergard, A.L. (1987). Episodic, semantic and procedural memory in a case of amnesia at an early age. Neuropsychologia, 25. 341-357.
-
-[[Depression]] - Poor performance on procedural memory tasks are associated with some forms of depression in homosexual/bisexual males who have HIV. Castellou. (1998). Apathy, depression and cognitive perform in HIV-1 infection. Neuropsychiatry and Clinical Neuroscience, 10 . "HIV attacks the immune system, resulting in a chronic, progressive illness" http://www.hc-sc.gc.ca/dc-ma/aids-sida/index-eng.php that can cause some suffers to become depressed. Depression, which is associated with an overall “feeling of helpless”, can involve both affective/cognitive symptoms (mood/emotional symptoms) and somatic (physical) symptoms. http://www.cmha.ca/BINS/content_page.asp?cid=3-86-87 Interestingly, increased levels of affective/cognitive symptoms of depression are associated with poorer performances on procedural learning tasks than if the individual had increased levels of somatic symptoms of depression. While the reason for the distinction in procedural learning deficits between affective and somatic symptoms is not yet completely understood, depression has been linked to involve a dysfunction of the basal ganglia, particularly the caudate nucleus which could explain why depression can be correlated with poorer performance on procedural tasks, but have no effect
-on episodic memory.
-
-==Disability and Procedural Memory==
-
-[[Williams syndrome]] (WS) is a genetic condition that is association with chromosomal mutations and several severe medical conditions such as facial and organ abnormalities, including damage to the basal ganglia and the cerebellum. Vicari, S., Bellucci, S., Carlesino G.A. (2001). Procedural learning distinct in children with Williams syndrome. Neuropsychologia, 39. 665-677 It also creates developmental challenges and has been linked to impaired procedural memory. In particular to procedural memory, children who suffer from WS will have problems solving any tasks that relies on temporal (time) sequencing. WS is different from Down syndrome (DS), a similar form of chromosomal mutation, in that individuals with DS will show impaired ability on explicit memory tests, but have no impairments in procedural memory. This is interesting because it suggests that the procedural learning deficits in WS children is not a universal symptom of all developmentally disabled individuals, but specific to this group. .
-
-==Procedural Memory and Aging==
-
-Just as disease and injury can affect various components of memory, aging does not affect memory unilaterally, but rather alters different forms of memory in different ways. It is difficult to ascertain a global effect of aging on procedural memory, as different neural components are responsible for various stages of skill acquisition (i.e. different regions of the brain are implicated in acquisition and proceduralization, or making an acquired skill automatic). However, a decline in the ability to remember and learn is fairly common in the elderly, including a decline in skill acquisition and reduced levels of performance in motor tasksKennedy, M.K, Raz,N. Age, Sex and Regional Brain Volumes Predict Perceptual-Motor Skill Acquisition. Cognition and Ageing Brain Though it would seem then that younger people are generally superior to older in skill acquisition (with some studies proving this to be true)Daselaar, S.M. (2003). Similar network activated by young and old adults during the acquisition of a motor sequence. Neurobiology of Aging, 24. 1013-1019,predominantly it has been established that no significant difference is found in the procedural memory of the young and old. This is because although younger brains acquire information quickly and efficiently, older individuals close the gap through practice. People in both younger and older age groups not only perform similarly on non-declarative learning tests, but also in the use of neuroimaging: fMRIs have shown that there is little difference in basal ganglia and cerebellum activity (the areas of the brain noted for procedural memory) for these age groups.
-This difference in procedural memory is not unlike the effects of amnesia- [[Alzheimer's]], a disease of progressive forgetting (among other symptoms)that is often associated with aging, also shows a remarkable retention in procedural learning ability. This preservation of procedural memory is interesting as well because of the decline in other forms of memory, namely declarativeYamadori, A. et al (1996). Procedural Memory in Alzheimer's Disease. Neurobiology of Aging, 17. 578.
-
-==Lesions, Injury and Procedural Memory==
-
-Overall the mechanisms responsible for procedural memory are poorly understood at present. However, it has been found that patients who have had portions of their medial temporal lobes surgically removed still have intact procedural memory.Budson, A.E., Prince, B.H. (2005). Memory Dysfunction. New England Journal of Medicine, 352. 692-699 For individuals who have lesions in the basal ganglia or cerebellum procedural memory will be affected, indicating that this area is critically involved in procedural memory. The importance of the basal ganglia and the cerebellum in procedural learning is supported by functional imagery which shows that the motor area, basal ganglia and cerebellum become active as a new task is being learned. Patients with tumors, strokes and other causes of damage to the basal ganglia or cerebellum provided further support for this finding as damage to those areas can leave patients with impaired procedural memory.
-''Children with [[Traumatic Brain Injury]]:'' Adults who suffer from Traumatic Brain Injury (TBI), show similar learning rates to those who do not have TBI Hanten, G., Dennis, M., Zhang, L., Barnes, M. (2004). Childhood Head Injury and Metacongitive Processes in Language and Memory. Developmental Neuropsychology, 25. 85-105. In considering a younger population, there has been some questions regarding the effect of pediatric traumatic brain injury on procedural memory. However, the study’s results have shown that consistent with literature on adult suffers of TBI, procedural memory will also be preserved in children with TBI. This result is most likely due to the fact that TBI tends to affect the anterior and medial regions of the brain opposed to the inferior regions which are responsible for implicit memory, including procedural learning and skill acquisition.
-
-=The Impact of Sleep on Procedural memory=
-
-Sleep cycles play critical roles in offline consolidation of memories.
-
-==== Consolidation ====
-
-Memory [[consolidation]] is a relatively poorly defined term in the literature for a series of cognitive processes that stabilize and enhance the efficacy of memory representations that are initially unstable when first formed. [[Encoding]], which takes information from short-term working memory and creates a memory trace for that information which is then consolidated into long-term memory, is rapid and is believed to occur across milliseconds. Encoding and consolidation appear to be distinct processes involving different molecular mechanisms, brain structures and regions, time courses as well as networks Stickgold, R., & Walker, M. P. (2007). Sleep-dependent memory consolidation and reconsolidation. Sleep Medicine, 8, 331-343. .
-
-The time required for memories to become consolidated is functionally related to the stability of those memories and their impermeability to interference. In addition, other similar memories can compete with a memory being consolidated and thus interfere. This interference through competition may actually serve as an advantage by allowing for the amendment of inaccurately formed memories prior to stabilization .
-
-==== Purpose of consolidation ====
-
-Behavioural facilitation:
-# Automatization: converting previously declarative memory representations to non-declarative procedural representations that require less conscious effort and fewer demands on brain structures such as the frontal lobes.
-# Extraction: taking information from a consolidated episodic memory and converting that information with the absence of episodic aspects (such as context and chronological information) into a semantic memory.
-# Integration: creating associations between related information .
-
-Consolidation enhances memories, which influence behaviour and performance in the absence of additional practice. In consolidation it appears as though long after stabilization has occurred enhancement of the memory continues to take place. In certain tasks, such as visual discrimination and procedural learning, enhancement appears to occur during sleep cycles. Consolidation also integrates newly formed memories into already established networks; sleep cycles appear to be critically involved in processes of memory integration and memory erasure .
-
-=== Sleep-Dependent Processes ===
-
-There are many stages of sleep and those stages are associated with the different stages of memory formation, encoding, consolidation and reconsolidation are associated Fogel, S. M., Carlyle, T. S., & Cote, K. A. (2007). Dissociable learning-dependent changes in REM and non-REM sleep in declarative and procedural memory systems. Behavioural Brain Research, 180, 48-61. .
-
-Phases of sleep:
-# Rapid eye movement (REM).
-# Non-rapid eye movement (NREM); this stage is divided into four sub-stages that are distinct in their role in sleep-dependent memory consolidation. Sub-stages 3 and 4 (the deepest form of sleep) are known as slow wave sleep (SWS) and have low frequency cortical oscillations (ranging from .5-4 Hz) .
-
-Sleep cycles such as REM, stage 2, and slow wave sleep (SWS) have been identified as stages critically involved in sleep-dependent processes. Distinct cortical activation has been correlated with those stages of sleep Stickgold, R. (2005). Sleep-dependent memory consolidation. Nature, 437, 1272-1278. .
-
-Sleep cycles are complex and vary depending on brain region, physiology, chemistry and experience. Different aspects and systems of memory consolidation can be influenced by different cycles of sleep, some of which appear crucial while others not . So-called ‘sleep-dependent processes’ are labeled thus because they are believed to take place during sleep cycles. However, this does not mean that they occur during sleep cycles only; wake cycles are also relevant and critical to those sleep-dependent processes . Wake cycles have been demonstrated to be involved in stabilization of procedural memories, distinguishing consolidation for explicit and implicit memory .
-
-Training itself can influence sleep cycle patterns and correlated brain activity with regions associated with the memories being enhanced (for example, there was observed improvement from overnight sleep associated with hippocampal activation during SWS after training for a spatial learning task). Critically, the features of the individual task to be learned are factors for sleep-dependent memory consolidation .
-
-=== Sleep and Procedural Memory Consolidation ===
-
-Procedural/ non-declarative memory appears to be associated more so with non-REM sleep and declarative memory appears to be more associated with REM sleep. However, REM sleep has been associated with enhancing the efficacy of memory consolidation for procedural memory, demonstrating that stages in sleep are not restricted to one type or aspect of memory consolidation .
-
-After a period of procedural memory training an increase in [[sleep spindles]] and rapid eye movements can be observed. There is also an increase in non-REM activity, which has typically been accepted as being deeper sleep .
-Non-REM activation may be associated with synaptic plasticity in the brain and may be related to the consolidation of procedural memory after training. In particular, stage 2 has been associated with procedural memory consolidation in Pursuit Rotor tasks- a simple, implicit motor skill task that does not necessitate the individual to adopt new strategies (which would require conscious effort and therefore by definition become explicit in nature) to improve in task performance. Some forms of declarative memory appears to be more correlated with increased REM theta wave activity, however this may depend on the nature of the task being learned .
-
-Individuals with lower skill levels for a particular task demonstrate more changes in REM sleep (which appear to be learning-dependent). In contrast individuals with greater skill levels for the same task appear to have more changes in stage 2 non-REM sleep. In other words when a skill is more challenging in its acquisition there are learning-dependent changes in REM sleep whereas when a skill is being refined then those learning-dependent changes are observed in stage 2 sleep .
-
-At present there is too little evidence to identify all the different types of post-encoding processes .
-
-Evidence from tasks such as visual texture discrimination, motor adaptation, and motor sequencing have supported that overnight sleep correlates to performance enhancement in those tasks, whereas the same time period where participants were awake did not Fischer, S., Hallschmid, M., Elsner, A. L., & Born, J. (2002). Sleep forms memory for finger skills. PNAS, 99(18), 11987-11991. Robertson, E. M., Pascual-Leone, A., & Press, D. Z. (2004). Awareness modifies the skill-learning benefits of sleep. Current Biology, 14, 208-212. Stickgold, R., James, L., & Hobson, J. A. (2000). Visual discrimination learning requires sleep after training. Nature Neuroscience, 3(12), 1237-1238. . However, this is not to imply that all memories have the potential to be enhanced during sleep cycles alone, irrespective of waking cycles. Sleep-dependent memory consolidation involves different stages of sleep depending on the nature of the memory and more than one stage of sleep may be involved in any particular memory’s consolidation .
-
-A caution for all studies that assess sleep’s impact on procedural memory is that fatigue, practice and circadian rhythms may affect performance . In addition, this research is correlationally based and therefore does not allow for inferences of causation. There are also issues with metaphor as the overarching theoretical paradigms used to describe cognitive phenomena risk researchers becoming caught up in definitions provided by the metaphor (and paradigm) and may result in the negligence of other critically involved factors.
-
-=Testing Procedural Memory=
-
-The testing of procedural memory is similar to that of any other type of memory. A variety of tests can be used.
-
-
-One type of procedural learning that can be measured is motor learning; through the use of such tests as pursuit rotor tracking and mirror tracing tasks.Kern, R.S., Green, M.F., Wallace, F.W., Charles, J. (1997). declarative and Procedural Learning in Schizophrenia. A Test of the Integrity of Divergent Memory Systems, 2. 39-50 Pursuit rotor tracking test requires subjects to maintain contact between the tip of a rod and a lit target, that moves in a circular path with the time on which the rod is on the target being measured. Various test trials are normally given with the speed of the target increasing after each trial. The mirror tracing task consists of an apparatus that involves a metal plate attached to a base, with another mirror plate attached vertically. A participant is asked to trace the image on the base, using feedback from the mirror image, as direct view is obstructed. The ratio of time on target and the total time to draw the image is what is measured.Van Gorp, W.G., Altshuler, L., Theberge, D.C., Mintz, J. (1999). Declarative and Procedural Memory in Bipolar Disorder, Biological psychiatry, 46. 525-531
-[[Image:Mirrortracing.jpg|thumb|Mirror Tracing Apparatus http://www.intropsych.com/ch07_cognition/measuring_hand_eye_coordination.html by Russ Dewey]]
-
-Cognitive procedural skills can also be measured through the use of the Tower of London. This task is modeled off of the oriental puzzle, the [[Tower of Hanoi]]. The Tower of London consists of a wooden base with 3 perpendicular sticks of varying length attached to it and three different coloured balls each with a hole in the center. To begin an examiner will arrange the balls in a certain order and then disrupt the pattern. The examinee will then have to remember the original pattern and reproduce it. . As trials continue the patterns become longer and more complicated. For example, the first trial may consist of just a three-pattern sequence of red ball, green ball, yellow ball. The next trial could be the first sequence (of red, green, yellow) and then another sequence of green, yellow, red. While each pattern only ever contains 3 different balls, a trial could contain many sets of patterns. Examinees gain performance points based on the amount of time it took them to get the sequence correct, with the assumption of the test being that if performance improves it is because the participant was learning the pattern and using procedural memory.
-
-Such test may be appropriate if it is suspected that impairments to procedural memory are the cause of a patients inability to learn new skills or the loss of previously learned skills Budson, A.C., Price, B.H. (2005). Memory Dysfunction. New England Journal of Medicine, 352. 692-699. Often patients may lose the ability to do common tasks that they could previous perform with ease such as playing an instrument or swinging a golf club. However, even with procedural memory damage it is possible to relearn these previously forgotten skills .
-

{{Life in the United Arab Emirates}}
-'''Telecommunications in the United Arab Emirates''' is under the control and supervision of the [[Telecommunications Regulatory Authority (UAE)|Telecommunications Regulatory Authority]] (TRA) which was established under UAE Federal Law by Decree No. 3 of 2003.[http://www.tra.ae/about_tra.html About TRA] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080612191934/http://www.tra.ae/about_tra.html |date=June 12, 2008 }} From 1976 to 2006 the [[Emirates Telecommunications Corporation]] (Etisalat) was the sole [[telephone]] and [[telecommunications]] provider for the [[United Arab Emirates|UAE]].[http://www.american.edu/carmel/jp2450a/3.htm American.edu - UAE ICT - Telecommunication Infrastructure, Regulation and Liberalization] And while there were exceptions for free zones and modern housing developments, for the majority of the UAE, Etisalat held a [[monopoly]] on business and personal telecommunications services. In February 2006 this monopoly became a [[duopoly]] when a new telephone company and Internet Service Provider, [[Emirates Integrated Telecommunications Company|du]] was established to offer mobile services across the UAE and Internet and TV services to some free zone areas.However, due to geographical distribution of service areas, the companies do not compete for customers and thus effectively operate as monopolies. Earlier [[Emirates Integrated Telecommunications Company|du]] provided [[Triple play (telecommunications)|triple play]] services to free zone areas under the name Emirates Integrated Telecommunications Company (EITC), which is still its legal name.
+'''Telecommunications in the United Arab Emirates''' is under the control and supervision of the [[Telecommunications Regulatory Authority (UAE)|Telecommunications Regulatory Authority]] (TRA) which was established under UAE Federal Law by Decree No. 3 of 2003.[http://www.tra.ae/about_tra.html About TRA] {{Wayback|date=20080612191934|url=http://www.tra.ae/about_tra.html|df=yes}} From 1976 to 2006 the [[Emirates Telecommunications Corporation]] (Etisalat) was the sole [[telephone]] and [[telecommunications]] provider for the [[United Arab Emirates|UAE]].[http://www.american.edu/carmel/jp2450a/3.htm American.edu - UAE ICT - Telecommunication Infrastructure, Regulation and Liberalization] And while there were exceptions for free zones and modern housing developments, for the majority of the UAE, Etisalat held a [[monopoly]] on business and personal telecommunications services. In February 2006 this monopoly became a [[duopoly]] when a new telephone company and Internet Service Provider, [[Emirates Integrated Telecommunications Company|du]] was established to offer mobile services across the UAE and Internet and TV services to some free zone areas.However, due to geographical distribution of service areas, the companies do not compete for customers and thus effectively operate as monopolies. Earlier [[Emirates Integrated Telecommunications Company|du]] provided [[Triple play (telecommunications)|triple play]] services to free zone areas under the name Emirates Integrated Telecommunications Company (EITC), which is still its legal name.

@@ -1 +1,377 @@\n
-{{pp-pc1}}
+{{pp-pc1|exiry=14 April 2013}}
+{{About||the 1953 novel of the same name by Louis Aragon|La Semaine Sainte|the 1995 Polish film|Holy Week (film)|the 2002 film|Semana santa (film)}}
+
+[[File:Folio 173v - The Entry into Jerusalem.jpg|thumb|300px|The [[Triumphal entry into Jerusalem|entry of Jesus into Jerusalem]] on [[Palm Sunday]] marks the beginning of Holy Week.]]
+{{Liturgical year}}
+
+'''Holy Week''' ([[Latin]]: ''Hebdomas Sancta'' or ''Hebdomas Maior'', "Greater Week"; [[Ancient Greek|Greek]]: ''Ἁγία καὶ Μεγάλη Ἑβδομάς'', ''Hagia kai Megale Hebdomas'') in [[Christianity]] is the last week of [[Lent]] and the week before [[Easter]]. It includes the religious holidays of [[Palm Sunday]], [[Maundy Thursday]] (Holy Thursday), [[Good Friday]], and [[Holy Saturday]]. It does not include [[Easter Sunday]]. In Eastern Orthodox tradition, Holy Week starts on [[Lazarus Saturday]], the day before Palm Sunday. (Easter Sunday, for context, is the first day of the new season of the Great Fifty Days, or [[Eastertide]], there being fifty days from Easter Sunday through Pentecost Sunday.) It is followed by [[Easter Week]].
+
+==History ==
+Holy Week in the [[Christian year]] is the week immediately before Easter. The earliest Catholic allusion to the custom of marking this week as a whole with special observances is to be found in the [[Apostolical Constitutions]] (v. 18, 19), dating from the latter half of the 3rd century and 4th century. In this text, abstinence from flesh is commanded for all the days, while for the Friday and Sunday an absolute fast is commanded. Dionysius Alexandrinus in his canonical epistle (AD 260), refers to the 91 fasting days implying that the observance of them had already become an established usage in his time.Apostolical Constitutions v. 18, 19
+
+There is some doubt about the genuineness of an ordinance attributed to [[Constantine I|Constantine]], in which abstinence from public business was enforced for the seven days immediately preceding [[Easter]] Sunday, and also for the seven which followed it; the ''[[Codex]] Theodosianus'', however, is explicit in ordering that all actions at law should cease, and the doors of all courts of law be closed during those 15 days (1. ii. tit. viii.). Of the particular days of the "great week" the earliest to emerge into special prominence was naturally Good Friday. Next came the ''Sabbatum Magnum'' ("Great Sabbath", i.e., [[Holy Saturday]] or Easter Eve) with its [[Paschal vigil|vigil]], which in the [[early church]] was associated with an expectation that the [[second advent]] would occur on an Easter Sunday.
+
+There are other [[Scriptures]] that refer to the traditions of the Early Church, most notably ''The Pilgrimage of Etheria'' (also known as ''The Pilgrimage of [[Egeria (pilgrim)|Egeria]]'') which details the complete observance of Holy Week in the early church.
+
+==Holy Week in Latin Rite Catholicism==
+
+===Palm Sunday (Passion Sunday)===
+{{Main|Palm Sunday}}
+Holy Week begins with what in the [[Roman Rite]] is now called Palm Sunday of the Passion of the Lord. Before 1955 it was known simply as Palm Sunday and the preceding Sunday as Passion Sunday. From 1955 to 1971 it was called Second Sunday in Passiontide or Palm Sunday.
+
+To commemorate the entrance of the messiah into [[Jerusalem]], to accomplish his [[paschal mystery]], it is customary to have before Mass a blessing of [[Arecaceae|palm leaves]] (or other branches, for example olive branches). The blessing ceremony, preferably held outside the church includes the reading of a Gospel account of how Jesus rode into Jerusalem humbly on a donkey, reminiscent of a Davidic victory procession, and how people placed palms on the ground in front of him. Immediately following this great time of celebration in the entering of Jesus into Jerusalemé, he begins his journey to the cross. This is followed by a procession or solemn entrance into the church, with the participants holding the blessed branches in their hands.
+
+The Mass itself includes a reading of the [[Passion (Christianity)|Passion]], the narrative of Jesus' capture, sufferings and death, as recounted in one of the [[Synoptic Gospels]].
+
+Before the reform of the rite by [[Pope Pius XI]], the blessing of the palms occurred inside the church within a service that followed the general outline of a Mass, with Collect, Epistle and Gospel, as far as the Sanctus. The palms were then blessed with five prayers, and a procession went out of the church and on its return included a ceremony for the reopening of the doors, which had meantime been shut. After this the normal Mass was celebrated.[http://www.sanctamissa.org/en/resources/missale-romanum.pdf 1920 typical edition of the Roman Missal]
+
+===Monday to Wednesday===
+The days between Palm Sunday and Holy Thursday are known as [[Holy Monday]], [[Holy Tuesday]], and [[Holy Wednesday]]. The Gospels of these days recount events not all of which occurred on the corresponding days between Jesus' entry into Jerusalem and his [[Last Supper]]. For instance, the Monday Gospel tells of the [[Anointing of Jesus|Anointing]] at [[Bethany (Biblical village)|Bethany]] ({{bibleverse||John|12:1-9}}), which occurred before the Palm Sunday event described in {{bibleverse||John|12:12-19}}.
+
+The [[Chrism]] Mass, whose texts the [[Roman Missal]] now gives under Holy Thursday, may be brought forward to one of these days, to facilitate participation by as many as possible of the clergy of the diocese together with the bishop. This Mass was not included in editions of the Roman Missal before the time of Pope Pius XII. In this Mass the bishop blesses separate oils for the sick (used in [[Anointing of the Sick]]), for [[catechumen]]s (used in [[Baptism]]) and [[chrism]] (used in Baptism, but especially in [[Confirmation]] and [[Ordination|Holy Orders]], as well as in rites such as the blessing of an altar and a church).
+
+===Tenebrae===
+When the principal services of Holy Thursday, Good Friday, and the Easter Vigil were celebrated in the morning, the office of [[Matins]] and [[Lauds]] of each day was celebrated on the evening of the preceding day in the service known as [[Tenebrae (liturgy)|Tenebrae]] (Latin, "Darkness").
+
+===Maundy (Holy) Thursday===
+{{Main|Mass of the Lord's Supper}}
+On this day the private celebration of [[Mass (liturgy)|Mass]] is forbidden.[http://www.saginaw.org/images/LITguide08_PARTII.pdf Holy Thursday: Number of Masses] Thus, apart from the [[Chrism]] Mass for the blessing of the Holy Oils that the diocesan bishop may celebrate on the morning of [[Maundy Thursday|Holy Thursday]], but also on some other day close to Easter, the only Mass on this day is the evening [[Mass of the Lord's Supper]], which inaugurates the period of three days, known as the [[Easter Triduum]], that includes [[Good Friday]] (seen as beginning with the service of the preceding evening), [[Holy Saturday]] and [[Easter]] Sunday up to [[Vespers|evening prayer]] on that day.[http://www.catholicliturgy.com/index.cfm/FuseAction/documentText/Index/2/SubIndex/38/ContentIndex/101/Start/97 General Norms for the Liturgical Year and the Calendar, 19]
+
+The Mass of the Lord's Supper commemorates the [[Last Supper]] of Jesus with his [[Twelve Apostles]], "the institution of the [[Eucharist]], the institution of the [[priesthood (Catholic Church)|priesthood]], and the [[The New Commandment|commandment]] of brotherly love that Jesus gave after washing the feet of his disciples."[http://www.catholicliturgy.com/index.cfm/FuseAction/documentText/Index/2/SubIndex/38/ContentIndex/324/Start/319 Holy Thursday Evening Mass of the Lord's Supper], 45
+
+All the bells of the church, including altar bells, may be rung during the ''[[Gloria in Excelsis Deo]]'' of the Mass (the Gloria is not traditionally sung during the entire Lenten season). The bells and the organ then fall silent until the Gloria at the [[Easter Vigil]]. {{Citation needed|date=November 2010}} In some countries, children are sometimes told: "The bells have flown to Rome."
+
+The Roman Missal recommends that, if considered pastorally appropriate, the priest should, immediately after the homily, celebrate the rite of [[Foot washing#Roman Catholic practice|washing the feet]] of an unspecified number of men, customarily twelve, recalling the number of the Apostles.
+
+A sufficient number of [[host (liturgy)|hosts]] are consecrated for use also in the Good Friday service, and at the conclusion the Blessed Sacrament is carried in procession to a place of reposition away from the main body of the church, which, if it involves an altar, is often called an "[[altar of repose]]".
+
+The altars of the church (except the one used for altar of repose) are later stripped quite bare and, to the extent possible, crosses are removed from the church or veiled. (In the pre-Vatican II rite, crucifixes and statues are covered with violet covers during Passion time, but the crucifix covers can be white instead of violet on Holy Thursday.)
+
+===Good Friday===
+{{Main|Good Friday}}
+Roman Catholic Christians treat Good Friday as a [[fasting|fast day]], which is defined as only having one full meal with, if needed, two small snacks that together do not make a full meal.
+
+The Catholic Good Friday in the [[Roman Rite]] afternoon service involves a series of readings and meditations, as well as the (sung) reading of the [[Passion (Christianity)|Passion]] account from the [[Gospel of John]] which is often read dramatically, with the priest, one or more readers, and the congregation all taking part. In the traditional Latin liturgy, the Passion is read by the priest facing the altar, with three deacons chanting in the sanctuary facing the people. Unlike Roman Catholic services on other days, the Good Friday service is not a [[Mass (liturgy)|Mass]], and in fact, celebration of Catholic Mass on Good Friday is forbidden. [[Eucharist]] consecrated the night before ([[Maundy Thursday|Holy Thursday]]) may be distributed. The [[cross]] is presented, with the people given an opportunity to [[veneration|venerate]] it. The services also include a long series of formal intercessions. The solemnity and somberness of the occasion has led to a phenomenon whereby in the course of history the liturgical provisions have a tendency to persist without substantial modification, even over the centuries. Some churches hold a three-hour mediation from midday, the [[Three Hours' Agony]]. In some countries, such as Malta, Philippines, Italy and Spain, processions with statues representing the Passion of Christ are held.
+[[Image:Quito Proc del Jesus del Gran Poder 2010 a.jpg|thumb|A Good Friday procession in Ecuador.]]
+
+* The Church mourns for Christ's death, reveres the Cross, and marvels at his life for his obedience until death.
+* The only sacraments celebrated are [[Sacrament of Penance (Catholic Church)|Penance]] and Anointing of the Sick. While there is no celebration of the Eucharist, Holy Communion is distributed to the faithful only in the Service of the Passion of the Lord, but can be taken at any hour to the sick who are unable to attend this service.
+* The altar remains completely bare, without texts, candlesticks, or altar cloths.
+* It is customary to empty the holy water fonts in preparation of the blessing of the water at the Easter Vigil.[http://www.catholicliturgy.com/index.cfm/FuseAction/LawText/Index/6/LawIndex/46 Letter of the Congregation for Divine Worship, 14 March 2003]
+* The [[Stations of the Cross]] are often prayed either in the church or outside.
+* The Celebration of the Passion of the Lord takes place in the afternoon, ideally at three o'clock, but for pastoral reasons a later hour may be chosen.
+* Since 1970, the colour of the vestments is red. Previously it was black. If a bishop celebrates, he wears a plain mitre.
+* 'The liturgy consists of three parts in the Roman Rite: the Liturgy of the Word, the Veneration of the Cross, and Holy Communion.
+:Liturgy of the Word
+::''Prostration'' of the celebrant before the [[altar]].
+::The ''readings'' from [[Book of Isaiah|Isaiah]] 53 (about the [[Isaiah 53|Suffering Servant]]) and the [[Epistle to the Hebrews]] are read.
+::The ''Passion narrative'' of the [[Gospel of John]] is sung or read, often divided between more than one singer or reader.
+::''General Intercessions'': The congregation prays for the Church, the Pope, the Jews, non-Christians, unbelievers and others.
+:''Veneration of the Cross'': A [[crucifix]] is solemnly unveiled before the congregation. The people venerate it on their knees. During this part, the "Reproaches" are often sung.
+:''Communion service'': Hosts consecrated at the Mass of the previous day are distributed to the people. (Before the reform of [[Pope Pius XII]], only the priest received Communion in the framework of what was called the "[[Mass of the Presanctified]]", which included the usual Offertory prayers, with the placing of wine in the chalice, but which omitted the [[Canon of the Mass]].)
+* Even if music is used in the Liturgy, it is not used to open and close the Liturgy, nor is there a formal recessional (closing procession).
+* It was once customary in some countries, especially England, to place a veiled [[monstrance]] with the [[Blessed Sacrament]] or a cross in a [[Easter Sepulchre|Holy Sepulchre]]".[http://www.ecclsoc.org/ritesofdurham.html The Easter Sepulchre Ceremony in Durham Abbey]; [http://www.elfinspell.com/AndrewsEaster.html ''Old Church Lore'' by William Andrews]
+* If crucifixes were covered starting with the next to last Sunday in Lent, they are unveiled without ceremony after the Good Friday service.
+
+===Holy Saturday===
+{{Main|Holy Saturday}}
+Mass is not celebrated on what is liturgically Holy Saturday. The celebration of [[Easter]] begins after sundown on what, though still Saturday in the civil calendar, is liturgically Easter Sunday.
+{{Quote|On Holy Saturday the Church waits at the Lord's tomb in prayer and fasting, meditating on his Passion and Death and on his Descent into Hell, and awaiting his Resurrection.
The Church abstains from the Sacrifice of the Mass, with the sacred table left bare, until after the solemn Vigil, that is, the anticipation by night of the Resurrection, when the time comes for paschal joys, the abundance of which overflows to occupy fifty days.Roman Missal, Holy Saturday}}
+
+In some Anglican churches, including the [[Episcopal Church in the United States]], there is provision for a simple liturgy of the word with readings commemorating the burial of Christ.
+
+The tabernacle is left empty and open. The lamp or candle usually situated next to the tabernacle denoting the Presence of Christ is put out, and the remaining [[Eucharist]]ic Hosts consecrated on Holy Thursday are kept elsewhere, usually the [[sacristy]], with a lamp or candle burning before it, so that, in cases of the danger of death, they may be given as ''[[viaticum]]''.
+
+===Easter Vigil===
+{{Main|Easter Vigil}}
+In the [[Roman Catholic]] tradition, the Easter Vigil, the longest and most solemn of the Catholic Church's liturgical services, lasting up to three or four hours, consists of four parts:
+# The Service of Light
+# The Liturgy of the Word
+# The Liturgy of Baptism: The sacraments of Baptism and Confirmation for new members of the Church and the Renewal of Baptismal Promises by the entire congregation.
+# [[Holy Eucharist]]
+
+The Liturgy begins after sundown on [[Holy Saturday]] as the crowd gathers inside the unlit church. In the darkness (often in a side chapel of the church building or, preferably, outside the church), a new fire is kindled and blessed by the priest. This new fire symbolizes the light of salvation and hope that God brought into the world through Christ's Resurrection, dispelling the darkness of sin and death. From this fire is lit the [[Paschal candle]], symbolizing the Light of Christ. This Paschal candle will be used throughout the season of Easter, remaining in the sanctuary of the Church or near the lectern, and throughout the coming year at baptisms and funerals, reminding all that that Christ is "light and life."
+
+[[Image:Maria Lichtmess.jpg|thumb|right|Candles lit for the Easter Vigil at [[Heiligenkreuz Abbey]] in Austria.]]
+All baptized Catholics present (i.e. those who have received the "Light of Christ") receive candles which are lit from the Paschal candle. As this symbolic "Light of Christ" spreads throughout those gathered, the darkness is decreased. A deacon, or the priest if there is no deacon, carries the Paschal Candle at the head of the entrance procession and, at three points, stops and chants the proclamation "Light of Christ" or "Christ our Light", to which the people respond "Thanks be to God." Once the procession concludes, the deacon or a cantor chants the [[Exultet]] (also called the "Easter Proclamation"), and, the church remaining lit only by the people's candles and the Paschal candle, the people take their seats for the Liturgy of the Word.
+
+The Liturgy of the Word consists of between two and seven readings from the [[Old Testament]]. The account of the Exodus is given particular attention in the readings since it is considered to be the Old Testament antetype of Christian salvation. Each reading is followed by a psalm and a prayer relating what has been read in the Old Testament to the Mystery of Christ. After these readings conclude, a fanfare may sound on the organ and additional musical instruments and the [[Gloria in Excelsis Deo]] is sung. During this outburst of musical jubilation the congregation's candles are extinguished, the church lights are turned on, and bells rung while the church's decorative funnings — altar frontals, the reredos, lectern hangings, processional banners, statues and paintings — which had been stripped or covered during Holy Week, are ceremonially replaced and unveiled and flowers are placed on altars and elsewhere. (In the pre-Vatican II rite, the statues, which have been covered during Passion Time, are unveiled at this time. In some places, the church removes the covering of statues and puts Easter flowers and decorations on the day of Holy Saturday before the Easter Vigil celebration. Also, in the current ritual the lights are turned on after the last proclamation of 'Christ our Light'.) Members of the congregation may have been encouraged to bring flowers which are also brought forward and placed about the sanctuary and side altars. A reading from the [[Epistle to the Romans]] is proclaimed. The [[Alleluia]] is sung for the first time since the beginning of Lent (or, in the pre-Vatican II rite, since Septuagesima). The [[Gospel]] of the Resurrection then follows, along with a homily.
+
+After the conclusion of the Liturgy of the Word, the water of the [[baptismal font]] is consecrated and any [[catechumen]]s or candidates for full communion are initiated into the church, by [[baptism]] and/or [[Confirmation (sacrament)|confirmation]], respectively. After the celebration of these sacraments of initiation, the congregation renews their baptismal vows and receive the sprinkling of [[holy water|baptismal water]]. The general intercessions follow.
+
+After the Liturgy of Baptism, the Liturgy of the [[Eucharist]] continues as usual. This is the first Mass of Easter Day. During the Eucharist, the newly baptised receive Holy Communion for the first time. According to the rubrics of the [[Missal]], the Eucharist should finish before dawn.
+
+===Easter Sunday===
+{{Main|Easter}}
+Easter Sunday, which immediately follows Holy Week, is the great feast day and apogee of the Christian liturgical year: on this day the Resurrection of Jesus Christ is celebrated. It is the first day of the new season of the Great Fifty Days, or [[Eastertide]], which runs from Easter Sunday to [[Pentecost]] Sunday. Easter Sunday is the main reason why Christians keep Sunday as the primary day of religious observance.
+
+===Notable Holy Week observances===
+Cities famous for their [[Holy Week procession]]s include:
+
+====Colombia====
+* [[Santa Cruz de Mompox]]
+* [[Popayán]]
+* [[Tunja]]
+* [[Pamplona, Colombia|Pamplona]]

+
+====Guatemala====
+* [[Antigua Guatemala]]
+* [[Guatemala City]]
+In Guatemala,Holy Week is celebrated with large processions with images. They last from Ash Wednesday to Easter Sunday.
+
+====Honduras====
+* [[Comayagua]]
+* [[Tegucigalpa]]
+
+====Indonesia====
+*[[Larantuka]]
+
+====Italy====
+[[Trapani]] holds one of the most elaborate processions for Holy Week anywhere in the world, culminating in the [[Processione dei Misteri di Trapani]] or simply the ''Misteri di Trapani'' (in English the ''Procession of the Mysteries of Trapani'' or the ''Mysteries of Trapani''), a day-long passion procession featuring twenty floats of lifelike wood, canvas and glue sculptures of individual scenes of the events of the Passion. The Misteri are amongst the oldest continuously running religious events in Europe, having been played every Good Friday since before the Easter of 1612, and running for at least 16 continuous hours, but occasionally well beyond the 24 hours; they are the longest religious festival in Sicily and in Italy. Similar but smaller or shorter passion processions are held in many other Sicilian cities, like [[Erice]] and [[Caltanissetta]], but also in various Southern Italian cities, like [[Salerno]] and [[Taranto]].
+
+====Malta====
+{{Main|Holy Week in Malta}}
+The Holy Week commemorations reach their paramount on Good Friday as the Catholic Church celebrates the passion of Jesus. Solemn celebrations take place in all churches together with processions in different villages around [[Malta]] and [[Gozo]]. During the celebration, the narrative of the passion is read in some localities. The Cross follows a significant Way of Jesus. Good Friday processions take place in [[Birgu]], [[Bormla]], [[Għaxaq]], [[Luqa]], [[Mosta]], [[Naxxar]], [[Paola, Malta|Paola]], [[Qormi]], [[Rabat]], [[Senglea]], [[Valletta]], [[Żebbuġ, Malta|Żebbuġ]] and [[Żejtun]]. Processions in Gozo will be in [[Nadur]], [[Victoria, Gozo|Victoria]], [[Xagħra]] Xewkija, and [[Żebbuġ, Gozo|Żebbuġ]].
+

+====Philippines====
+{{Main|Holy Week in the Philippines}}
+In the predominantly Catholic [[Philippines]], Maundy Thursday and Good Friday are national holidays; work is suspended in government offices and private businesses. Most stores are closed and most people in the cities head to the provinces for the long Easter weekend.
+
+Holy Week is commemorated with street processions, the [[Way of the Cross]], and a [[Passion play]] called the Sinakulo. The Church keeps the day solemn by not tolling the church bells, and no mass will be celebrated. In some communities (most famously in [[City of San Fernando, Pampanga|San Fernando]], [[Pampanga]]), the processions include devotees who self-flagellate and sometimes even have themselves nailed to crosses as expressions of penance. After three o'clock in the afternoon of Good Friday (the time at which Jesus is traditionally believed to have died), noise is discouraged, some [[radio|radio stations]] and [[television|television stations]] sign off (while others remain signed-on, broadcasting Religious Programming), businesses automatically close, and the faithful are urged to keep a solemn and prayerful disposition through to [[Easter]] Sunday.
+
+At [[Mass]] on [[Palm Sunday]], Catholics carry "palaspas" or palm leaves to be blessed by the priest. Many Filipinos bring home the palm leaves after the Mass and place these above their front doors or their windows, believing that doing so can ward off evil spirits. Holy Monday marks the beginning of the Pabasa (literally, reading) or [[Pasyon]], the marathon chanting of the story of Jesus' life, passion, and death, which continues day and night, for as long as two straight days. A popular Holy Thursday tradition is the ''Bisita Iglesia'' (Church Visit), which involves visiting several Churches at which the faithful would pray the [[Stations of the Cross]]. The last Mass before [[Easter]] is also celebrated on Holy Thursday, usually including a reenactment of the [[Washing of the Feet]] of the [[Twelve Apostles|Apostles]]; this Mass is followed by the procession of the [[Blessed Sacrament]] before it is taken to the [[Altar of Repose]]. [[Good Friday]] in the Philippines is commemorated with street processions, the [[Way of the Cross]], the commemoration of Jesus' [[Seven last words]] (Siete Palabras) and a Passion play called the [[Passion play|Sinakulo]].
+
+Easter morning is marked with joyous celebration, the first being the dawn [[Salubong]], wherein large statues of Jesus and Mary are brought in procession together to meet, imagining the first reunion of Jesus and his mother Mary after Jesus' [[Resurrection]]. This is followed by the joyous Easter Mass.
+
+====Spain====
+{{Main|Holy Week in Spain}}
+
+[[Málaga]], [[Seville]], [[Madrid]], [[Valladolid]], [[Zamora, Spain|Zamora]] and [[León, Spain|León]] hold elaborate processions for Holy Week. A tradition that dates from [[Middle Ages|medieval times]] which has spread to other cities in [[Andalusia]], the ''"Semana Santa en Sevilla"'' is notable for featuring the procession of '''"pasos"''', lifelike wood or plaster sculptures of individual scenes of the events that happened between Jesus' arrest and his burial, or images of the Virgin Mary showing grief for the torture and killing of her son. In Málaga the lifelike wooden or plaster sculptures are called "tronos" and they are carried through the streets by penitents dressed in long purple robes, often with pointed hats, followed by women in black carrying candles for up to 11 hours. These pasos and tronos are physically carried on the necks of ''costaleros'' (literally "sack men", because of the ''costal'', a sack-like cloth that they wear over their neck, to soften the burden) or "braceros" (this name is popular in Leon), and can weigh up to five metric tonnes. The pasos are set up and maintained by ''hermandades'' and ''cofradías'', religious brotherhoods that are common to a specific area of the city, whose precede the paso dressed in Roman military costumes or penitential robes. Those members who wish to do so wear these penitential robes with conical hats, or ''[[capirotes]]'', used to conceal the face of the wearer. These "Nazarenos" or "Papones" (this word it´s typical from Leon) carry processional candles, may walk the city streets barefoot, and may carry shackles and chains in their feet as penance. A brass band, marching band, a drum and bugle band, or in Málaga's case a military band (such as that of the [[Spanish Legion]] or other military units) may accompany the group, playing funeral marches, hymns or "marchas" written for the occasion.
+
+====Venezuela====
+* [[Miranda (state)|Miranda]]
+** [[Tacarigua de Mamporal]]
+** [[Guatire]]
+* [[Caracas]]
+

+* [[:vi:Tuần Thánh|Tuần Thánh]]
